Here's the issue: ```cuda for (int c_in = 0; c_in < C; ++c_in) { // All threads write to in_sm for (int p = tid; p < smem_len; p += THREADS) { ... in_sm[p] = val; } __syncthreads(); // All threads read from in_sm for (...) { ... float v0 = in_sm[l]; ... } __syncthreads(); // This is necessary before the next iteration writes to in_sm! } ``` YES! The `__syncthreads()` at the end of the `c_in` loop is necessary to ensure all threads finish reading `in_sm` before the next iteration starts writing to it. I HAVE this `__syncthreads()`. Good. But what about the `if (l >= L) break;` inside the compute loop? Threads that break early finish the compute loop and reach the ending `__syncthreads()`. Threads that don't break also eventually finish and reach `__syncthreads()`. This is fine. Now, for the weight loading into shared memory, I had: ```cuda for (int idx = tid; idx < w_total; idx += THREADS) { ... w_sm[idx] = wval; } __syncthreads(); ``` This was at the beginning of the kernel. All threads need to finish before any thread reads `w_sm`. But some threads might have `tid >= w_total` (e.g., if w_total=6144 and tid=6144..1023). Wait, tid ranges 0..1023. w_total=6144. Then `__syncthreads()` ensures all writes are visible before computation starts. Good. After the first `__syncthreads()`, `w_sm` is never modified again. Actually, let me look at one thing I haven't checked: the reduction kernel. ```cuda __global__ void reduce_mean_rstd_kernel(...) { int b = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; ... for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { sum += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, sum, offset); sum_sq += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, sum_sq, offset); } __shared__ float ssum[32]; __shared__ float ssq[32]; int lane = tid % 32; int warp_id = tid / 32; int num_warps = blockDim.x / 32; if (lane == 0) { ssum[warp_id] = sum; ssq[warp_id] = sum_sq; } __syncthreads(); if (warp_id == 0) { ... } } ``` Wait! After the warp reduction, threads in warp 0 execute `if (warp_id == 0) { ... }`. What about threads in other warps (warp_id > 0)? They skip this block and the kernel returns. But there's a `__syncthreads()` inside the `if (warp_id == 0)` block! Oh no! `__syncthreads()` inside a conditional block where the condition diverges between warps is ILLEGAL in CUDA. If some threads in a block reach `__syncthreads()` and others don't, it causes undefined behavior, usually a deadlock/hang! In my reduction kernel: ```cuda if (warp_id == 0) { float ws = (lane < num_warps) ? ssum[lane] : 0.0f; ... for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { ws += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, ws, offset); ... } if (lane == 0) { mean[b] = m; rstd[b] = rstd_val; } // NO __syncthreads() here, good! } ``` Wait, let me re-read my reduction kernel carefully. Actually, looking back at my code: ```cuda __syncthreads(); if (warp_id == 0) { float ws = (lane < num_warps) ? ssum[lane] : 0.0f; float wsq = (lane < num_warps) ? ssq[lane] : 0.0f; for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { ws += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, ws, offset); wsq += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, wsq, offset); } if (lane == 0) { float m = ws / N; float m2 = wsq / N; float var = m2 - m * m; if (var < 0.0f) var = 0.0f; mean[b] = m; rstd[b] = rsqrtf(var + 1e-5f); } } ``` There's NO `__syncthreads()` inside the `if (warp_id == 0)` block! The `__syncthreads()` is BEFORE the `if (warp_id == 0)`. Then the kernel ends after the `if` block. So threads with warp_id > 0 execute: 1. `__syncthreads()` 2. Skip the `if (warp_id == 0)` block 3. Kernel returns Threads with warp_id == 0 execute: 1. `__syncthreads()` 2. Execute the `if` block 3. Kernel returns All threads in the block reach `__syncthreads()`. All threads reach the end of the kernel. There is no divergence around `__syncthreads()`. BUT WAIT, in the FULLY-FUSED main kernel, I have: ```cuda if (lpt > MAX_LPT) return; ... __syncthreads(); ``` As I discussed earlier, `lpt` is the same for all threads in a block (it's based on L and THREADS, both constants). So either ALL threads return or NONE return. No divergence. This is fine. OK, so there's no `__syncthreads()` divergence issue in my kernels. The timeout remains unexplained. UNLESS... there's a `__syncthreads()` divergence in the fully-fused kernel that I missed. Let me look at the fully-fused kernel again: ```cuda template <int MAX_LPT> __global__ void fused_block_forward_kernel(...) { ... int lpt = (L + THREADS - 1) / THREADS; if (lpt > MAX_LPT) return; ... for (int c_in = 0; c_in < C; ++c_in) { for (int p = tid; p < smem_len; p += THREADS) { ... in_sm[p] = val; } __syncthreads(); for (int i = 0; i < lpt; ++i) { int l = tid + i * THREADS; if (l >= L) break; ... } __syncthreads(); } ... } ``` Ah! Here it is! The `if (l >= L) break;` INSIDE a loop that is BEFORE a `__syncthreads()`. If lpt=4 and L=4096, then: - For i=0: l = tid, all < 4096, no break - For i=1: l = tid + 1024, all < 4096, no break - For i=2: l = tid + 2048, all < 4096, no break - For i=3: l = tid + 3072. Since tid < 1024, l < 4096. No break. So for L=4096 and THREADS=1024, the `break` is NEVER taken. All threads execute the full loop. No divergence. But what about other configurations where L is not a multiple of THREADS? The problem states L=4096, THREADS=1024, so it's exact. But if the evaluator tests with different sizes, it might trigger the divergence issue. However, the problem says the parameters are fixed. Actually, the evaluation might test with the exact parameters given, or it might test with slight variations. But since the problem specifies exact values, I'd assume those are the test values. Wait, `compile_kernel` and `run_correctness` use the exact parameters from the problem. So L=4096, B=32, C=256. For these values, the `break` is never taken. So the timeout is still unexplained. One more thought: maybe the timeout isn't from my CUDA kernel at all. Maybe it comes from Python-level overhead, like `load_inline` doing a full recompilation every time the module is imported. If `load_inline` is called inside `forward()`, it would recompile every forward pass. In my code, I call `get_cuda_ext()` which has a global cache, so it should only compile once. But what if the cache is somehow not working? In my `get_cuda_ext()` function: ```python _cuda_ext = None def get_cuda_ext(): global _cuda_ext if _cuda_ext is None: _cuda_ext = load_inline(...) return _cuda_ext ``` This should cache the extension. Let me combine these optimizations: ```python class ModelNew(nn.Module): def forward(self, x): residual = x x = x.contiguous() # Pre-extract parameters to avoid ModuleList overhead # For each of the 9 layers mean = torch.empty(x.size(0), device=x.device, dtype=x.dtype) rstd = torch.empty(x.size(0), device=x.device, dtype=x.dtype) for i in range(9): norm = self.norms[i] conv = self.convs[i] d = 2 ** i # Launch custom reduction kernel cuda_ext.launch_reduce_mean_rstd(x, mean, rstd) # Launch custom elementwise norm+gelu kernel tmp = torch.empty_like(x) cuda_ext.launch_norm_gelu(x, mean, rstd, norm.weight, norm.bias, tmp) # PyTorch conv x = conv(tmp) # Fused add kernel or PyTorch add x = x + residual return x ``` The temporal cost: - 9 custom reductions (fast) - 9 custom norm+gelu (1 kernel each, fused) - 9 conv1d (cuDNN) - 9 adds (PyTorch) Total: 36 kernel launches, same as reference. CUDA source for reduction: ```cuda __global__ void reduce_mean_rstd_kernel(const float* __restrict__ x, float* __restrict__ mean, float* __restrict__ rstd, int B, int C, int L) { int b = blockIdx.x; int tid = threadIdx.x; int N = C * L; const float* xb = x + b * N; float sum = 0.0f; float sum_sq = 0.0f; for (int i = tid; i < N; i += blockDim.x) { float v = xb[i]; sum += v; sum_sq += v * v; } for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { sum += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, sum, offset); sum_sq += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, sum_sq, offset); } __shared__ float ssum[32]; __shared__ float ssq[32]; int lane = tid % 32; int warp_id = tid / 32; int num_warps = blockDim.x / 32; if (lane == 0) { ssum[warp_id] = sum; ssq[warp_id] = sum_sq; } __syncthreads(); if (warp_id == 0) { float ws = (lane < num_warps) ? ssum[lane] : 0.0f; float wsq = (lane < num_warps) ? ssq[lane] : 0.0f; for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) { ws += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, ws, offset); wsq += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, wsq, offset); } if (lane == 0) { float m = ws / N; float m2 = wsq / N; float var = m2 - m * m; if (var < 0.0f) var = 0.0f; mean[b] = m; rstd[b] = rsqrtf(var + 1e-5f); } } } ``` CUDA source for fully-fused main kernel: ```cuda __global__ void fused_block_forward_kernel(const float* __restrict__ x, const float* __restrict__ residual, const float* __restrict__ norm_w, const float* __restrict__ norm_b, const float* __restrict__ conv_w, const float* __restrict__ conv_b, const float* __restrict__ mean, const float* __restrict__ rstd, float* __restrict__ out, int B, int C, int L, int K, int dilation) { const int C_OUT_PER_BLOCK = 4; const int THREADS = 256; int b = blockIdx.x; int c_out_tile = blockIdx.y; int c_out_start = c_out_tile * C_OUT_PER_BLOCK; int tid = threadIdx.x; int lpt = (L + THREADS - 1) / THREADS; extern __shared__ float smem[]; int smem_len = L + 2 * dilation; float* in_sm = smem; float* w_sm = smem + smem_len; int w_total = C * K * C_OUT_PER_BLOCK; for (int idx = tid; idx < w_total; idx += THREADS) { int c_local = idx % C_OUT_PER_BLOCK; int tmp = idx / C_OUT_PER_BLOCK; int k = tmp % K; int c_in = tmp / K; int c_out = c_out_start + c_local; float wval = 0.0f; if (c_out < C) { wval = conv_w[((c_out * C) + c_in) * K + k]; } w_sm[idx] = wval; } __syncthreads(); float m = mean[b]; float rs = rstd[b]; int x_base = b * C * L; float acc[16][C_OUT_PER_BLOCK]; // max lpt for THREADS=256, L<=4096 -> lpt<=16 #pragma unroll for (int i = 0; i < 16; ++i) { #pragma unroll for (int c = 0; c < C_OUT_PER_BLOCK; ++c) { acc[i][c] = 0.0f; } } for (int c_in = 0; c_in < C; ++c_in) { for (int p = tid; p < smem_len; p += THREADS) { int pos = p - dilation; float val = 0.0f; if (pos >= 0 && pos < L) { val = x[x_base + c_in * L + pos]; val = (val - m) * rs; val = val * norm_w[c_in * L + pos] + norm_b[c_in * L + pos]; val = val * 0.5f * (1.0f + erff(val * 0.70710678118f)); } in_sm[p] = val; } __syncthreads(); for (int i = 0; i < lpt; ++i) { int l = tid + i * THREADS; if (l >= L) continue; float v0 = in_sm[l]; float v1 = in_sm[l + dilation]; float v2 = in_sm[l + 2 * dilation]; #pragma unroll for (int c = 0; c < C_OUT_PER_BLOCK; ++c) { int widx0 = (c_in * K + 0) * C_OUT_PER_BLOCK + c; int widx1 = (c_in * K + 1) * C_OUT_PER_BLOCK + c; int widx2 = (c_in * K + 2) * C_OUT_PER_BLOCK + c; acc[i][c] += w_sm[widx0] * v0 + w_sm[widx1] * v1 + w_sm[widx2] * v2; } } __syncthreads(); } for (int i = 0; i < lpt; ++i) { int l = tid + i * THREADS; if (l >= L) continue; #pragma unroll for (int c = 0; c < C_OUT_PER_BLOCK; ++c) { int c_out = c_out_start + c; if (c_out < C) { float val = acc[i][c] + conv_b[c_out] + residual[x_base + c_out * L + l]; out[x_base + c_out * L + l] = val; } } } } ``` Wait, the `acc` array is declared as `float acc[16][C_OUT_PER_BLOCK]`. The custom kernel takes x, mean, rstd, weight, bias and computes the normalized+scaled+biased+GELU output. For mean and rstd, I use PyTorch's native functions. This is: 1. Marginally faster (saves one kernel launch and some dispatch overhead) Code: ```python class ModelNew(nn.Module): def forward(self, x): x = x.contiguous() residual = x ext = get_cuda_ext() for norm, conv in zip(self.norms, self.convs): # Compute mean and var with PyTorch mean = x.mean(dim=[1,2], keepdim=True) var = x.var(dim=[1,2], keepdim=True, unbiased=False) rstd = torch.rsqrt(var + 1e-5) # Custom kernel for norm + gelu tmp = torch.empty_like(x) ext.launch_norm_gelu(x, mean, rstd, norm.weight, norm.bias, tmp) # PyTorch conv x = conv(tmp) # Add residual x = x + residual return x ``` The custom kernel is very simple and fast: ```cuda __global__ void norm_gelu_kernel(const float* x, const float* mean, const float* rstd, const float* w, const float* b, float* out, int B, int C, int L) { int idx = blockIdx.x * blockDim.x + threadIdx.x; int total = B * C * L; if (idx >= total) return; int b = idx / (C * L); int rem = idx % (C * L); int c = rem / L; int l = rem % L; float v = x[idx]; v = (v - mean[b]) * rstd[b]; v = v * w[c * L + l] + b[c * L + l]; v = v * 0.5f * (1.0f + erff(v * 0.70710678118f)); out[idx] = v; } ``` Grid: ceil(B*C*L / 1024) = ceil(33554432 / 1024) = 32768 blocks. Block: 1024 threads. This kernel is fully coalesced and very fast. For performance: this saves one kernel launch per layer (fusing norm's elementwise + affine + gelu into one kernel, vs PyTorch's norm + gelu which is 2 kernels). Actually, PyTorch's LayerNorm already fuses reduction + elementwise + affine into one kernel. The GELU is a separate kernel. But the dilation makes the gather operation non-trivial. And calling cuBLAS from a custom kernel isn't straightforward (you'd need to call it from host code). What if I use `torch.matmul` with a explicit gather? For each layer, I can gather the dilated input into a shape (B, C, L, 3) tensor: ```python padded = F.pad(x, (d, d)) indices = torch.arange(L, device=x.device).unsqueeze(0) + torch.tensor([-d, 0, d], device=x.device).unsqueeze(1) gathered = padded[:, :, indices] # shape (B, C, L, 3) ``` Then conv is a matmul: ```python output = torch.einsum('bclk,ock->bol', gathered, conv.weight) output = output + conv.bias.unsqueeze(-1) ``` This uses optimized GEMM, which is very fast. But the gather operation might be slow. Actually, `gathered = padded[:, :, indices]` uses advanced indexing, which creates a copy. For L=4096 and C=256, this is 32*256*4096*3 = 100M elements = 400MB. At 3TB/s, the copy takes ~130 microseconds. Not terrible. But the GEMM is: (B*L, C*3) @ (C*3, C) with B*L=131072 and C*3=768 and C=256. GEMM dimensions: M=131072, K=768, N=256. Total FLOPs: 2*M*N*K = 2*131072*256*768 = 51.5 GFLOPs. At 100 TFLOPS (Tensor Cores with FP32 accumulation), this takes ~0.5ms. Total per layer: gather (0.13ms) + GEMM (0.5ms) = 0.63ms. For 9 layers: ~5.7ms. The reference using cuDNN might be faster or slower depending on the dilation. For small d, cuDNN is probably faster because it uses specific direct conv kernels. For large d, the gather+GEMM approach might be faster. But the gather requires creating large intermediate tensors, which uses memory. For 9 layers, this is 9*400MB = 3.6GB of temporary allocations. This might be slow due to memory allocation overhead. And the numerical accuracy? The gather+GEMM approach uses cuBLAS, which might use TF32 or different accumulation order. The accuracy might differ from the reference. So this approach is risky. OK, final decision: I'll write the custom kernel that fuses the entire block (norm + gelu + conv + add) into one kernel, but I'll use explicit loops and shared memory. I'll use block size 256 and C_OUT=8. Why? Because: 1. It's the most performant approach if it works. 2. The correctness differences might pass if I use the exact same formulas. 3. The timeout might have been a transient issue. Let me write this carefully and double-check everything. Wait, one more optimization: instead of computing mean and rstd in a separate kernel, I can compute them inside the main kernel! How? If each block processes all channels for one batch and some positions, the block can compute the mean and rstd by having threads reduce across all positions while loading activations. Actually, for the main kernel, each block only processes a subset of channels. The reduction needs to be across ALL channels and positions. So a per-block reduction wouldn't give the global mean/var. Unless I use a separate reduction phase within each block, but that only works if each block processes all channels. With C_OUT_PER_BLOCK=8, each block processes only 8 channels out of 256. It can't compute the mean/var. So the reduction must be done separately beforehand. But what if I assign each block to process ALL channels for a small set of positions, and use the entire block to compute mean/var? For example, block size 1024, each block processes one batch. The 1024 threads collectively process all 256*4096 elements to compute mean/var, storing in shared memory. Then the same block computes the conv. This would eliminate the separate reduction kernel launch! But each block would process the entire batch, which means only 32 blocks total (one per batch). With 132 SMs, only 32 blocks run, leaving 100 SMs idle. Bad utilization. To process multiple batches per SM, I'd need more blocks. But each block processes one batch. So 32 blocks total. That's not enough to saturate the GPU. Alternatively, I can process a batch in multiple blocks. For example, 32 blocks per batch, each processing 8 channels. But then each block can't compute the mean/var for the whole batch independently. Unless I use a two-pass approach: 1. Pass 1: Each block computes partial sums for a subset of elements. Store partial sums in global memory. 2. Pass 2: Read partial sums, compute final mean/var, then compute norm+gelu+conv. But this is essentially what I already have with the separate reduction kernel. One more idea: atomic operations for reduction. Each thread adds to global atomic counters. But this serializes the adds and would be very slow for 32M elements. So separate reduction kernel is the way to go. Final plan: 1. Reduction kernel: 32 blocks, 1024 threads each. 2. Main kernel: 32 batches * 32 channel tiles = 1024 blocks, 256 threads each. This is a reasonable configuration. Let me write the code and submit it. If the timeout happens again, at least I tried. Here's my final, carefully written kernel code. One more thing: I should note that the CUDA kernel handles the case where `lpt` exceeds the template parameter by returning early. But I also need to handle cases where `lpt` is smaller. The loop `for (int i = 0; i < lpt; ++i)` handles this naturally. The extra elements in `acc` are just unused. For the compile-time array `float acc[16][8]`, if lpt < 16, only `acc[0..lpt-1]` are used. The rest are initialized to 0 but never read. This is fine. However, initializing 128 floats per thread with `#pragma unroll` might generate a lot of instructions. For lpt=16 (actual value), all 128 elements are initialized. For the problem, this is exactly what happens. OK, I need to be careful with the `#pragma unroll` on the initialization. With 16*8=128 iterations, fully unrolled might generate 128 `mov` instructions. This is acceptable. But if the compiler also unrolls the `for (int c = 0; c < C_OUT_PER_BLOCK; ++c)` loops, there are multiple nested unrolls. This might generate large code, but it should be fine. Let me finalize and submit.

import torch
import torch.nn as nn
from torch.utils.cpp_extension import load_inline

CPP_SOURCE = r'''
#include <torch/extension.h>
void launch_reduce_mean_rstd(const torch::Tensor& x, torch::Tensor& mean, torch::Tensor& rstd);
void launch_fused_block_forward(const torch::Tensor& x,
                               const torch::Tensor& residual,
                               const torch::Tensor& norm_w,
                               const torch::Tensor& norm_b,
                               const torch::Tensor& conv_w,
                               const torch::Tensor& conv_b,
                               const torch::Tensor& mean,
                               const torch::Tensor& rstd,
                               torch::Tensor& out,
                               int dilation);
'''

CUDA_SOURCE = r'''
#include <torch/extension.h>
#include <cuda_runtime.h>
#include <math.h>

__global__ void reduce_mean_rstd_kernel(const float* __restrict__ x,
                                        float* __restrict__ mean,
                                        float* __restrict__ rstd,
                                        int B, int C, int L) {
    int b = blockIdx.x;
    int tid = threadIdx.x;
    int N = C * L;
    const float* xb = x + b * N;

    float sum = 0.0f;
    float sum_sq = 0.0f;
    for (int i = tid; i < N; i += blockDim.x) {
        float v = xb[i];
        sum += v;
        sum_sq += v * v;
    }

    for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) {
        sum += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, sum, offset);
        sum_sq += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, sum_sq, offset);
    }

    __shared__ float ssum[32];
    __shared__ float ssq[32];
    int lane = tid % 32;
    int warp_id = tid / 32;
    int num_warps = blockDim.x / 32;
    if (lane == 0) {
        ssum[warp_id] = sum;
        ssq[warp_id] = sum_sq;
    }
    __syncthreads();

    if (warp_id == 0) {
        float ws = (lane < num_warps) ? ssum[lane] : 0.0f;
        float wsq = (lane < num_warps) ? ssq[lane] : 0.0f;
        for (int offset = 16; offset > 0; offset /= 2) {
            ws += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, ws, offset);
            wsq += __shfl_down_sync(0xffffffff, wsq, offset);
        }
        if (lane == 0) {
            float m = ws / N;
            float m2 = wsq / N;
            float var = m2 - m * m;
            if (var < 0.0f) var = 0.0f;
            mean[b] = m;
            rstd[b] = rsqrtf(var + 1e-5f);
        }
    }
}

static __device__ __forceinline__ float gelu_exact(float x) {
    return x * 0.5f * (1.0f + erff(x * 0.70710678118654752440f));
}

template <int MAX_LPT>
__global__ void fused_block_forward_kernel(const float* __restrict__ x,
                                          const float* __restrict__ residual,
                                          const float* __restrict__ norm_w,
                                          const float* __restrict__ norm_b,
                                          const float* __restrict__ conv_w,
                                          const float* __restrict__ conv_b,
                                          const float* __restrict__ mean,
                                          const float* __restrict__ rstd,
                                          float* __restrict__ out,
                                          int B, int C, int L, int K, int dilation) {
    const int C_OUT_PER_BLOCK = 8;
    const int THREADS = 256;

    int b = blockIdx.x;
    int c_out_tile = blockIdx.y;
    int c_out_start = c_out_tile * C_OUT_PER_BLOCK;
    int tid = threadIdx.x;

    int lpt = (L + THREADS - 1) / THREADS;
    if (lpt > MAX_LPT) return;

    extern __shared__ float smem[];
    int smem_len = L + 2 * dilation;
    float* in_sm = smem;
    float* w_sm = smem + smem_len;

    int w_total = C * K * C_OUT_PER_BLOCK;
    for (int idx = tid; idx < w_total; idx += THREADS) {
        int c_local = idx % C_OUT_PER_BLOCK;
        int tmp = idx / C_OUT_PER_BLOCK;
        int k = tmp % K;
        int c_in = tmp / K;
        int c_out = c_out_start + c_local;
        float wval = 0.0f;
        if (c_out < C) {
            wval = conv_w[((c_out * C) + c_in) * K + k];
        }
        w_sm[idx] = wval;
    }
    __syncthreads();

    float m = mean[b];
    float rs = rstd[b];
    int x_base = b * C * L;

    float acc[16][C_OUT_PER_BLOCK];
    #pragma unroll
    for (int i = 0; i < MAX_LPT; ++i) {
        #pragma unroll
        for (int c = 0; c < C_OUT_PER_BLOCK; ++c) {
            acc[i][c] = 0.0f;
        }
    }

    for (int c_in = 0; c_in < C; ++c_in) {
        for (int p = tid; p < smem_len; p += THREADS) {
            int pos = p - dilation;
            float val = 0.0f;
            if (pos >= 0 && pos < L) {
                val = x[x_base + c_in * L + pos];
                val = (val - m) * rs;
                val = val * norm_w[c_in * L + pos] + norm_b[c_in * L + pos];
                val = gelu_exact(val);
            }
            in_sm[p] = val;
        }
        __syncthreads();

        for (int i = 0; i < lpt; ++i) {
            int l = tid + i * THREADS;
            if (l >= L) continue;
            float v0 = in_sm[l];
            float v1 = in_sm[l + dilation];
            float v2 = in_sm[l + 2 * dilation];
            #pragma unroll
            for (int c = 0; c < C_OUT_PER_BLOCK; ++c) {
                int widx0 = (c_in * K + 0) * C_OUT_PER_BLOCK + c;
                int widx1 = (c_in * K + 1) * C_OUT_PER_BLOCK + c;
                int widx2 = (c_in * K + 2) * C_OUT_PER_BLOCK + c;
                acc[i][c] += w_sm[widx0] * v0 + w_sm[widx1] * v1 + w_sm[widx2] * v2;
            }
        }
        __syncthreads();
    }

    for (int i = 0; i < lpt; ++i) {
        int l = tid + i * THREADS;
        if (l >= L) continue;
        #pragma unroll
        for (int c = 0; c < C_OUT_PER_BLOCK; ++c) {
            int c_out = c_out_start + c;
            if (c_out < C) {
                float val = acc[i][c] + conv_b[c_out] + residual[x_base + c_out * L + l];
                out[x_base + c_out * L + l] = val;
            }
        }
    }
}

void launch_reduce_mean_rstd(const torch::Tensor& x, torch::Tensor& mean, torch::Tensor& rstd) {
    int B = x.size(0);
    int C = x.size(1);
    int L = x.size(2);
    const float* x_ptr = x.data_ptr<float>();
    float* m_ptr = mean.data_ptr<float>();
    float* r_ptr = rstd.data_ptr<float>();
    reduce_mean_rstd_kernel<<<B, 1024>>>(x_ptr, m_ptr, r_ptr, B, C, L);
}

void launch_fused_block_forward(const torch::Tensor& x,
                               const torch::Tensor& residual,
                               const torch::Tensor& norm_w,
                               const torch::Tensor& norm_b,
                               const torch::Tensor& conv_w,
                               const torch::Tensor& conv_b,
                               const torch::Tensor& mean,
                               const torch::Tensor& rstd,
                               torch::Tensor& out,
                               int dilation) {
    int B = x.size(0);
    int C = x.size(1);
    int L = x.size(2);
    int K = conv_w.size(2);

    const int THREADS = 256;
    const int C_OUT_PER_BLOCK = 8;

    int lpt = (L + THREADS - 1) / THREADS;

    dim3 grid(B, (C + C_OUT_PER_BLOCK - 1) / C_OUT_PER_BLOCK);
    dim3 block(THREADS);

    int smem_len = L + 2 * dilation;
    int w_size = C * K * C_OUT_PER_BLOCK;
    size_t shared_mem = (smem_len + w_size) * sizeof(float);

    const float* x_ptr = x.data_ptr<float>();
    const float* res_ptr = residual.data_ptr<float>();
    const float* nw_ptr = norm_w.data_ptr<float>();
    const float* nb_ptr = norm_b.data_ptr<float>();
    const float* cw_ptr = conv_w.data_ptr<float>();
    const float* cb_ptr = conv_b.data_ptr<float>();
    const float* m_ptr = mean.data_ptr<float>();
    const float* r_ptr = rstd.data_ptr<float>();
    float* o_ptr = out.data_ptr<float>();

    if (lpt <= 16) {
        fused_block_forward_kernel<16><<<grid, block, shared_mem>>>(x_ptr, res_ptr, nw_ptr, nb_ptr, cw_ptr, cb_ptr, m_ptr, r_ptr, o_ptr, B, C, L, K, dilation);
    } else {
        // fallback not reached for fixed parameters
        fused_block_forward_kernel<32><<<grid, block, shared_mem>>>(x_ptr, res_ptr, nw_ptr, nb_ptr, cw_ptr, cb_ptr, m_ptr, r_ptr, o_ptr, B, C, L, K, dilation);
    }
}
'''

_cuda_ext = None

def get_cuda_ext():
    global _cuda_ext
    if _cuda_ext is None:
        _cuda_ext = load_inline(
            name="fused_dilated_conv_final",
            cpp_sources=CPP_SOURCE,
            cuda_sources=CUDA_SOURCE,
            functions=["launch_reduce_mean_rstd", "launch_fused_block_forward"],
            extra_cuda_cflags=["-O3"],
            verbose=False,
        )
    return _cuda_ext

class ModelNew(nn.Module):
    def __init__(self, channels, seq_len, kernel_size, max_dilation_power):
        super(ModelNew, self).__init__()
        self.channels = channels
        self.seq_len = seq_len
        self.kernel_size = kernel_size
        self.max_dilation_power = max_dilation_power
        self.norms = nn.ModuleList()
        self.convs = nn.ModuleList()
        for i in range(max_dilation_power + 1):
            dilation = 2 ** i
            self.norms.append(nn.LayerNorm([channels, seq_len]))
            self.convs.append(nn.Conv1d(channels, channels, kernel_size,
                                        padding=dilation, dilation=dilation))

    def forward(self, x):
        x = x.contiguous()
        residual = x
        curr = x
        B, C, L = curr.shape
        ext = get_cuda_ext()
        for i in range(self.max_dilation_power + 1):
            dilation = 2 ** i
            norm = self.norms[i]
            conv = self.convs[i]
            mean = torch.empty(B, device=curr.device, dtype=curr.dtype)
            rstd = torch.empty(B, device=curr.device, dtype=curr.dtype)
            ext.launch_reduce_mean_rstd(curr, mean, rstd)
            out = torch.empty_like(curr)
            ext.launch_fused_block_forward(
                curr, residual,
                norm.weight, norm.bias,
                conv.weight, conv.bias,
                mean, rstd,
                out,
                dilation,
            )
            curr = out
        return curr
